Eggeling
  1. Having brought water forward 3, he takes out (the material for) a cake on eleven potsherds for Agni and Vishс╣Зu; for Agni is all the deities, since it is in Agni that offering is made to all the deities. Moreover Agni is the lower half, and Vishс╣Зu is the upper half of the sacrifice: ‘I will become consecrated after encompassing all the deities, after encompassing the entire sacrifice,’ thus he thinks, and hence there is a cake on eleven potsherds for Agni and Vishс╣Зu.

  1. Some then offer a rice-pap to the ─Аdityas. This is referred to (in the passage, Rig-veda X, 72, 8), ‘There are eight sons of Aditi who were born from her body; with seven she went to the gods, but M─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Нa 4 she cast off.’

Eggeling
  1. Now Aditi had eight sons. But those that are called ’the gods, sons of Aditi,’ were only seven, for the eighth, M─Бrt─Бс╣Зс╕Нa, she brought forth unformed 7: it was a mere lump of bodily matter 8, as broad as it was high. Some, however, say that he was of the size of a man.

Eggeling
  1. The gods, sons of Aditi, then spake, ‘That

which was born after us 9 must not be lost: come, let us fashion it.’ They accordingly fashioned it as this man is fashioned. The flesh which was cut off him, and thrown down in a lump, became the elephant: hence they say that one must not accept an elephant (as a gift) 10, since the elephant has sprung from man. Now he whom they thus fashioned was Vivasvat, the ─Аditya (or the sun); and of him (came) these creatures.

Eggeling
  1. He spake, ‘Among my offspring he shall be successful who shall offer that rice-pap to the ─Аdityas.’ Accordingly he alone succeeds who offers that rice-pap to the ─Аdityas. Only that (cake) to Agni and Vishс╣Зu is, however, generally approved.

Eggeling
  1. There are seventeen kindling-verses for it 13. In a low voice he offers to the two deities. There are five fore-offerings and three after-offerings. For the sake of completeness they perform the patn─лsaс╣Бy─Бjas 14; but he offers no samishс╣нayajus, lest, having put on that garment of the consecrated, he should reach the end of the sacrifice before its completion; for the samishс╣нayajus is the end of the sacrifice.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

Eggeling
  1. He (the sacrificer) then gets himself anointed (with fresh butter), while standing east of the hall. For, having been flayed, man is sore; and by getting himself anointed, he becomes healed of his soreness: for man’s skin is on the cow, and that fresh butter

also comes from the cow. He (the Adhvaryu) thus supplies him with his own skin, and for this reason he gets himself anointed.

Eggeling
  1. It is fresh butter,–for melted butter (ghee) belongs to the gods, and creamy butter 17 to men. Here, on the other hand, it is neither ghee nor creamy butter; it should rather be both ghee and creamy butter, for the sake of unimpaired vigour: by means of that which is of unimpaired vigour he accordingly makes him of unimpaired vigour.

Eggeling
  1. He anoints him from the head down to the feet in accordance with the tendency of the hair, with the text (V─Бj. S. IV, 3), ‘Thou art the sap of the great ones.’ The ‘great ones,’ doubtless, is one of the names of those cows, and their sap indeed it is: therefore he says, ’thou art the sap of the great ones.’ ‘Thou art life-giving: give me light!’ There is nothing obscure in this.

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he anoints the eyes. ‘Sore, indeed, is the eye of man; mine is sound,’ so spake Y─Бj├▒avalkya. Dim-eyed, indeed, he was (heretofore); and the secretion of his eyes was matter. He now makes his eyes sound by anointing them.

Eggeling
  1. Now, when the gods slew the Asura-Rakshas, ┼Ъushс╣Зa 21, the D─Бnava, falling backward entered into the eyes of men: he is that pupil of the eye, and

looks like a young lad 22. Against him he (the sacrificer), now that he enters on the sacrifice, raises a rampart of stone all round himself, for the ointment is (produced from) stone.

Eggeling
  1. It is such as comes from mount Trikakud; for when Indra slew Vr╠еtra he transformed that eye of his (Vr╠еtra’s) into the mount Trikakud 27. The reason, then, why (ointment) from mount Trikakud (is used), is that he thereby puts eye into eye. Should he be unable to obtain any Traikakuda ointment, any other than Traikakuda may be used; for one and the same, indeed, is the significance of the ointment.

Eggeling
  1. He anoints (the eyes) with a reed-stalk, for the reed is a thunderbolt. It is one with a tuft, in order to chase away the evil spirits 28. For rootless,

indeed, and unfettered on both sides, the Rakshas roams along the air; even as man here roams along the air 29, rootless and unfettered on both sides: the reason, then, why it is (a reed-stalk) with a tuft, is to chase away the evil spirits.

Eggeling
  1. He anoints it with the text, ‘Thou art the eye-ball of Vr╠еtra,’–for Vr╠еtra’s eye-ball it indeed is;–‘Eye-giving thou art: give me the eye!’ in this there is nothing obscure.

Eggeling
  1. The right eye he anoints once with the sacrificial formula, once silently; and the left one he anoints once with the formula, twice silently: thus he makes the left (or upper) one superior 30.

Eggeling
  1. He then purifies him with a cleanser (pavitra, strainer) of sacred grass; for impure, indeed, is man:–he is foul within in that he speaks untruth;–and sacred grass is pure: ‘Having become pure, I shall be consecrated,’ thus he thinks;–and the stalks of sacred grass are a means of cleansing,–

‘Having become cleansed, I shall be consecrated,’ thus he thinks; and therefore he purifies him with a cleanser of sacred grass.

рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╢реЗрд╖рднреВрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рджреНрд░реЗрдгреЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердорд╛рд╣- рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рджреНрд░реЗрдгреЗрддрд┐ 35 ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкрд╡рдирд╛рддреН ‘рдПрд╖рдГ’ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдГ ‘рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рджреНрд░рдВ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдореН’ рее реиреи рее

Eggeling
  1. He purifies him with seven (stalks) each time, with the text (V─Бj. S. IV, 4), ‘May the Lord of thought purify me!’ The lord of thought doubtless is Praj─Бpati 36: he thereby means to say, ‘May Praj─Бpati purify me!’ ‘May the lord of speech purify me!’ The lord of speech doubtless is Praj─Бpati 37: he thereby means to say, ‘May Praj─Бpati purify me!’ ‘May the divine Savitr╠е purify me,’–for well purified indeed is he whom the divine

Savitr╠е has purified 38; therefore he says, ‘May the divine Savitr╠е purify me!’–‘with a flawless cleanser;’ for that blower (the wind) is indeed a flawless cleanser: ‘with that one,’ he means to say; ‘with the rays of the sun;’ for they, the rays of the sun, are indeed purifiers; therefore he says, ‘with the rays of the sun.’

Eggeling
  1. ‘O Lord of the pavitra’ (means of purification),–for he (who is consecrated) is indeed the lord of the pavitra,–‘of thee, purified by the pavitra,–for he is indeed purified by the pavitra;–‘with whatsoever desire I purify myself, may I be able to effect it!’ whereby he says, ‘May I reach the end of the sacrifice!’

Eggeling
  1. He then makes him pronounce the beginning of the benedictions (V─Бj. S. IV, 5), ‘We approach you, O gods, for desirable goods, at the opening of the sacrifice; we call on you, O gods, for holy 39 blessings.’ Thereby the officiating priests invoke on him those blessings which are their own.

Eggeling
  1. He (the sacrificer) then bends his fingers inwards, viz. the two (little fingers), with the text (V─Бj. S. IV, 6), ‘Hail, from the mind (I take hold of) the sacrifice!’–the two (nameless or ring fingers) with, ‘Hail, from the wide ether!’–the two (middle fingers) with, ‘Hail, from the sky and earth!’–with, ‘Hail, from the wind, I take hold (of the sacrifice)!’ he clenches both fists 41. Not visibly

indeed is the sacrifice to be taken hold of, as is either this staff or the garment,–but invisible indeed are the gods, invisible is the sacrifice.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рд╕ рдпрджрд╛рд╣реЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрдореН ред рд╡рд╛рддрд╛рджрд╛рд░рднреЗ- рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд╛рддреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЗрди рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ’ рд╡рд╛рддреЛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ’ ред ‘рд╡реИ’- рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди “рд╡рд╛рддреЛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрддрд╛рдореН”- рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рд░реНрджреНрдпреЛрддреНрдпрддреЗ рее реирем рее

Eggeling
  1. Now when he says, ‘Hail, from the mind (I take hold of) the sacrifice,’ he takes hold of it from the mind;–in saying, ‘From the wide ether,’ he takes hold of it from the ether;–in saying, ‘From heaven and earth,’ he takes hold of it from those two, heaven and earth, on which this entire universe rests;–and in saying, ‘From the wind I take hold of (the sacrifice)’–the wind being the sacrifice–he takes hold of the sacrifice directly.

рдПрдХрджреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рд╜рд╡реНрдпрдпрдорд┐рджрдВ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ ред ‘рдпрддреН’ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН ‘рд╕:’ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ ‘рдПрдЬрддрд┐ рддреНрд╡рддреН’ рдЪрд▓рддрд┐ рдЪ, ‘рдкрд░реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрддреЗ рддреНрд╡рддреН’ рдкрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рдорддрд┐ рдЪ; рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (рей-рез-рей)

Eggeling
  1. He (the Adhvaryu) then makes him enter the hall. He walks along the back of the ─Аhavan─лya and the front of the G─Бrhapatya 47,–this is his passage until the Soma pressing. The reason why this is his passage until the Soma pressing is this. The fire is the womb of the sacrifice, and the consecrated is an embryo; and the embryo moves about

within the womb. And since he (the sacrificer) moves about there (between the fires), and now turns round and now back, therefore these embryos move about, and now turn round and now back. Hence this is his passage till the Soma pressing.

  22. 15:1 Sa esha kan─лnakaс╕е kum─Бraka iva paribh─Бsate. A play on the word kan─лnaka, which has the double meaning of ‘youth’ and ‘pupil of the eye.’ The St. Petersburg Dict. assigns also to kum─Бraka the meaning of ‘ball of the eye’ in this (the only) passage. The K─Бс╣Зva recension reads, Sa esha kum─Бraka iva kan─лnak─Бy─Бm (? both ‘maiden’ and ‘pupil of the eye’). ↩︎

  28. 15:3 Professor Delbr├╝ck, S. F. III, 27, takes it thus, ‘He brushes the eye with the end of a reed, for the reed is a thunderbolt capable of repelling mischief.’ But, if ‘virakshast─Бyai’ belonged to what precedes, it would probably have to be construed with ‘┼Ыareshikay─Б тАЩnakti,’ the clause with ‘vai,’ giving the reason, being inserted parenthetically; while, in an idiomatic rendering, it would have to be placed at the end: He anoints the eyes with a reed-stalk in order to chase away the evil spirits, the reed being a thunderbolt. This abstract dative of purpose is very common; it being generally construed with what precedes, as, for instance, I, 1, 4, 1; 3, 2, 8; 5, 3, 8; 15; III, 1, 2, 13; 19; ; and, with a parenthetic clause with ‘vai’ intervening, III, 2, 1, 13; IV, 5, 7, 7. Not less common is the analogous construction with a clause with ’ned’ (’lest such an event should happen’) instead of the dative of the abstract, cf. I, 2, 1, 8; 9; IV, 5, 9, 3. ↩︎

  29. 16:1 I now take this passage differently from my interpretation of I, 1, 2, 4 (‘and, in order that this man may move about the air, rootless and unfettered in both directions’). See also IV, 1, 1, 20. ↩︎

  30. 16:2 ‘Tad uttaram evaitad uttar─Бvat karoti;’ ‘uttar─Б╠Бm ├йvaitad ├║ttaram karoti,’ K─Бс╣Зva recension. Cf. p. 2, note 1. ↩︎

  31. 17:1 See part i, p. 19, note 2. ↩︎

  32. 17:2 The Taitt. S. VI, 1, 1 allows the option between (one), 2, 3, 5, 6, 7, 9, and 21 stalks; while the Ait. Br. I, 3 mentions only the highest number. ↩︎
